**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

*   **Topic 2.1: Aggressive New Tariffs and International Trade Disruption**

    The White House has unilaterally enacted significant and disruptive new trade policies with immediate, far-reaching market impacts. First, the long-standing "de minimis" tariff exemption for global low-cost goods and small packages has been officially terminated. This action is widely expected to increase the direct cost burden on American consumers by applying tariffs to a vast new category of imported goods [1]. Alongside this, the administration has imposed a universal 50% tariff on all copper imports, a move that caused the metal's global price to plunge immediately upon announcement [2].

    These protectionist measures have drawn sharp warnings from the economic community. One Dartmouth College economics professor has labeled the administration's strategy a "tariff disaster," citing historical precedent [3]. While there is some evidence that the U.S. economy grew more than expected as the tariffs took effect, this data is clouded by a separate, alarming report from The Wall Street Journal. The investigation asserts that U.S. inflation data now relies "more on guesswork than previously known," raising fundamental questions about the integrity of the key federal metrics used to guide economic policy [4, 5].

### 1.2 Accusations of Politicization and Irregular Appointments
The administration faces multiple, mounting accusations of politicizing government functions and breaking with established norms for senior appointments. A prominent report claims President Trump has "weaponized the government to replace ‘wokeness’ with his version of diversity," signaling a systematic overhaul of federal initiatives [1]. This charge is compounded by public allegations from government scientists, who assert that a new official climate report "twists their work," suggesting direct political manipulation of federal scientific findings [2]. At the Department of Defense, Secretary Pete Hegseth’s office has publicly and preemptively dismissed a Pentagon review of the "Signalgate" controversy as nothing more than a "'political witch hunt'" [3].

These actions are mirrored by breaks from tradition in personnel decisions. In what is described as "another break from the norm," President Trump is personally interviewing candidates for 4-star general positions, inserting himself directly into a process typically managed within the military hierarchy [4]. Concurrently, the administration has quietly appointed a new head for the national parks system who reportedly possesses "no experience" in the relevant field, raising alarms about the stewardship of key federal lands and agencies [5].

**References:**
[1] Trump has weaponized the government to replace ‘wokeness’ with his version of diversity, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/30/politics/dei-anti-woke-trump-administration-analysis  
[2] Scientists Say New Government Climate Report Twists Their Work, https://www.wired.com/story/scientists-say-new-government-climate-report-twists-their-work/

## 2. Economic Policy & Trade

### 2.1 Aggressive New Tariffs and International Trade Disruption
The White House has unilaterally enacted significant and disruptive new trade policies with immediate, far-reaching market impacts. First, the long-standing "de minimis" tariff exemption for global low-cost goods and small packages has been officially terminated. This action is widely expected to increase the direct cost burden on American consumers by applying tariffs to a vast new category of imported goods [1]. Alongside this, the administration has imposed a universal 50% tariff on all copper imports, a move that caused the metal's global price to plunge immediately upon announcement [2].

These protectionist measures have drawn sharp warnings from the economic community. One Dartmouth College economics professor has labeled the administration's strategy a "tariff disaster," citing historical precedent [3]. While there is some evidence that the U.S. economy grew more than expected as the tariffs took effect, this data is clouded by a separate, alarming report from The Wall Street Journal. The investigation asserts that U.S. inflation data now relies "more on guesswork than previously known," raising fundamental questions about the integrity of the key federal metrics used to guide economic policy [4, 5].

**References:**
[1] Trump ends de minimis exemption for global low-cost goods, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/30/trump-de-minimis-shipping.html  
[2] Trump slaps universal 50% tariff on copper imports; metal's price plunges, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/30/trump-copper-tariff-trade.html  
[3] Trump’s Tariff Disaster | Doug Irwin, an economics professor at Dartmouth College, on Trump’s trade war, the myth of protectionism, and what history teaches us about tariffs, https://www.theatlantic.com/podcasts/archive/2025/07/david-frum-show-tariffs-trump-doug-irwin/683707/  
[4] US economy grew more than expected as Trump’s tariffs took hold, https://abcnews.go.com/amp/Business/us-economy-expected-grown-trumps-tariffs-hold/story?id=124183248  
[5] U.S. Inflation Data Rely More on Guesswork Than Previously Known, https://www.wsj.com/articles/u-s-inflation-data-rely-more-on-guesswork-than-previously-known-e19e21f9  

### 2.2 Clashes Over Fiscal and Monetary Policy
Significant policy disagreements are erupting between the White House and other key economic bodies, as well as within the administration itself. The Federal Reserve has held interest rates steady, a decision publicly characterized as "defying Trump" and his repeated calls for a rate cut. The decision by the board was not unanimous, with two governors dissenting from the majority opinion, indicating internal divisions at the central bank [1, 2].

In an extraordinary instance of internal dissent, a major administration proposal for newborn savings accounts has been met with extraordinary public criticism from Treasury Secretary Scott Bessent. The Secretary characterized the plan as a "'back door for privatizing Social Security,'" a politically explosive charge coming from a sitting cabinet member [3]. Separately, the state of Colorado is facing a major budget crisis, with officials reporting a $1 billion shortfall directly attributed to the fiscal consequences of a recent federal tax overhaul [4].

## 3. Elections & Party Politics

### 3.1 National Redistricting Battle Ignites Between Texas and California
A high-stakes conflict over congressional redistricting is escalating into a national fight with significant implications for the balance of power in the House. Republicans in Texas have unveiled a proposed gerrymandered House map explicitly designed to "please Trump," which projections indicate could add five new GOP seats to the state's delegation [1]. In a direct and combative response, Gavin Newsom has announced that California will move to redraw its own congressional map if the Texas plan proceeds, teeing up an unprecedented state-vs-state proxy war over representation [2]. The feud has rapidly grown personal, with reports of public taunts between Newsom and Vice President JD Vance, with Newsom quoted as challenging Vance, "'Try Again, Dumb Dumb'" [3]. This proposed Texas map is expected to force a painful political "reckoning" for incumbent Democratic representatives in the southern part of the state [4].

### 3.2 Political Violence and Party Strategy Debates
An extreme act of targeted political violence has occurred in Virginia, where a city councilman was attacked at his workplace, doused with gasoline, and set on fire [1]. At this time, headlines provide no information regarding a motive or potential suspects in the attack.

Meanwhile, internal debates over Democratic party strategy are intensifying. A new poll indicates that Democratic leadership is "totally lost touch" with its base on the issue of Israel, where popular support for the country has fallen to an "all-time low" [2]. Prominent party figures like Pete Buttigieg are publicly advising that Democrats must end what he calls "'preachy' politics" in order to effectively combat the Trump administration's agenda [3]. On the electoral front, former Vice President Kamala Harris has now officially ruled out a run for governor of California [4]. Additionally, there is renewed "chatter" surrounding a potential Supreme Court nomination for incumbent Utah Senator Mike Lee [5].

## 4. Domestic Affairs & Agency Actions

### 4.1 Major Shifts in Health, Immigration, and Justice Policies
The administration is initiating several controversial and transformative domestic policies. A new private health tracking system is being launched with the direct assistance of "Big Tech" firms, raising immediate questions about data privacy and government surveillance [1]. This policy announcement occurs amidst significant upheaval at the FDA, where the newly appointed vaccine chief has resigned after serving for less than three months. The resignation is amplified by recently ousted members of a federal vaccine panel who now publicly assert that "rigorous science is being abandoned" by the agency, fueling a crisis of confidence [2, 3].

On immigration, the administration has authorized the deployment of the National Guard to U.S. Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) facilities [4]. This move comes as one Ohio city, whose Haitian migrant population was recently disparaged by President Trump, braces to defend its residents against potential deportation actions [5]. Furthermore, a report indicates the Trump administration has signaled an intention to begin "locking up homeless people" as a matter of policy, a stark and controversial declaration [6].

### 4.2 Clashes Over Environmental, Education, and Disaster Aid Funding
Federal agencies are implementing policies that are generating significant and targeted pushback. The EPA, under the leadership of Administrator Lee Zeldin, is facing public backlash and denouncements from New Yorkers for its decision to roll back the agency's critical "climate endangerment finding," a foundational environmental policy [1]. In disaster response, North Carolina officials report that recovery efforts from Hurricane Helene are being actively and materially hindered by FEMA's denial of federal aid claims, creating friction between state and federal authorities [2]. In the education sector, Brown University has reached a formal agreement with the Trump administration to resolve unspecified discrimination complaints. This deal restores the institution's access to federal research funding, which had presumably been withheld pending the resolution [3].

## 5. Legislative Branch: Congress

### 5.1 Bipartisan Stock Ban Advances Amid Partisan Fights
A bipartisan legislative effort to ban stock trading by members of Congress is gaining momentum, with Republican Senator Josh Hawley notably voting with Democrats to advance the bill from committee [1]. This rare moment of cross-party cooperation contrasts sharply with deepening partisan divides on other legislative and oversight conflicts. Democrats are launching another attempt to revive the Voting Rights Act but reportedly face "long odds" of success in the current Republican-controlled Congress [2].

In oversight matters, House Democrats have escalated their conflict with the executive branch by filing a lawsuit against ICE, alleging that the agency illegally barred their members from entering and inspecting its detention facilities [3]. Separately, Senator Bernie Sanders has launched a formal investigation into Secretary of Health and Human Services Robert F. Kennedy Jr., citing the Secretary's public "attacks on vaccine access" as the impetus for the high-profile inquiry [4].

## 6. Foreign Policy & National Security

### 6.1 Controversial Sanctions, Intelligence Disputes, and Human Rights Scrutiny
U.S. foreign policy actions are generating significant international controversy. The Treasury Department has officially sanctioned Alexandre de Moraes, a sitting Brazilian judge. Reports describe this move as a direct response to the judge’s role in prosecuting Jair Bolsonaro, a key international political ally of President Trump, suggesting a politicized use of sanctions power [1].

Within the U.S. intelligence community, a rare public dispute has erupted. A former CIA agent has directly pushed back against Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard after she publicly accused former President Obama of participating in a "'treasonous conspiracy'" against President Trump [2]. These events unfold as the United States itself has been "highlighted" on an international human rights watchlist. The headline does not specify which organization issued the watchlist or the precise reasons for the U.S. inclusion, but the designation itself is a notable blow to the nation's international standing [3].

**References:**

## 7. Civil Rights & Constitutional Issues

### 7.1 Court Battles Over Press Freedom and LGBTQ+ Rights
Significant legal battles and social conflicts over core constitutional rights are underway. A federal court has delivered a major victory for press freedom, ruling that the government cannot bar Associated Press journalists from attending White House events and has ordered their immediate reinstatement [1]. In a separate First Amendment issue, protest organizers are planning a nationwide "'Rage Against the Regime'" event for August 2, signaling growing grassroots opposition [2].

On LGBTQ+ rights, a new analysis reveals a stark reality: more than one in four transgender people in the U.S. now live in one of the 19 states that have enacted restrictive "bathroom bans" [3]. In Colorado, a Christian bookstore, reportedly in partnership with a "hate group," has filed a lawsuit against the state's Kelly Loving Act. The suit seeks a First Amendment right to misgender people, directly challenging state-level anti-discrimination protections [4].
